[25:35] And he brought him unto him: and when the spirit saw him, immediately  it beat him about; and he fell upon the ground, and was raging and foaming.

[25:36] And Jesus asked his father, How long is the time during which he hath been thus? He  said unto him, From his youth until now.

[25:37] But, my Lord, help me wherein thou  canst, and have mercy upon me.

[25:38] Jesus said unto him, If thou canst believe! All  things are possible to him that believeth.

[25:39] And immediately the father of the child  cried out, weeping, and said, I believe, my Lord; help my lack of faith.

[25:40] And when Jesus saw the hastening of the people, and their coming at the sound, he rebuked that unclean spirit, and said to it, Thou dumb spirit that speakest not, I command  thee, come out of him, and enter not again into him.

[25:41] And that spirit, devil, cried out much, and bruised him, and came out; and that child fell as one dead, and  many thought that he had died.

[25:42] But Jesus took him by his hand, and raised him  up, and gave him to his father; and that child was healed from that hour.

[25:43] And the people all marvelled at the greatness of God.

[25:44] And when Jesus entered into the house, his disciples came, and asked him  privately, and said unto him, Why were we not able to heal him? Jesus said unto Arabic, p.

[25:45] them, Because of your unbelief.

[25:46] Verily I say unto you, If ye have faith as a grain of mustard seed, ye shall say to this mountain, Remove hence;  and it shall remove; and nothing shall overcome you.

[25:47] But it is impossible to cast out this kind by anything except by fasting and prayer.

[25:48] And when he went forth thence, they passed through Galilee: and he would not  that any man should know it.

[25:49] And he taught his disciples, and said unto them,  Keep ye these sayings in your ears and your hearts: for the Son of man is to be delivered into the hands of men, and they shall kill him; and when he is killed, he  shall rise on the third day.

[25:50] But they knew not the word which he spake unto them, for it was concealed from them, that they should not perceive it; and they feared to  ask him about this word.

[25:51] And they were exceeding sorrowful.

[26:1] Section XXV.

[26:2] And in that day this thought presented itself to his disciples, and they said, which  haply should be the greatest among them.

[26:3] And when they came to Capernaum, and entered into the house, Jesus said unto them, What were ye considering in the  way among yourselves? And they were silent because they had considered that matter.

[26:4] And when Simon went forth without, those that received two dirhams for the tribute came to Cephas, and said unto him, Doth your master not give his two  dirhams? He said unto them, Yea.

[26:5] And when Cephas entered the house, Jesus anticipated him, and said unto him, What thinkest thou, Simon? the kings of the earth, from whom do they receive custom and tribute? from their sons, or from  Arabic, p.

[26:6] strangers? Simon said unto him, From strangers.

[26:7] Jesus said unto him, Children then are free.

[26:8] Simon said unto him, Yea.

[26:9] Jesus said unto him,  Give thou also unto them, like the stranger.

[26:10] But, lest it trouble them, go thou to the sea, and cast a hook; and the first fish that cometh up, open its mouth, and thou shalt find a stater: take therefore that, and give for me and thee.

[26:11] And in that hour came the disciples to Jesus, and said unto him, Who, thinkest  thou, is greater in the kingdom of heaven? And Jesus knew the thought of their heart, and called a child, and set him in the midst, and took him in his arms, and  said unto them, Verily I say unto you, If ye do not return, and become as children,  ye shall not enter the kingdom of heaven.

[26:12] Every one that shall receive in my name such as this child hath received me: and whosoever receiveth me receiveth  not me, but him that sent me.

[26:13] And he who is little in your company, the same  shall be great.

[26:14] But whosoever shall injure one of these little ones that believe in me, it were better for him that a great millstone should be hanged about his neck, and he should be drowned in the depths of the sea.

[26:15] John answered and said, Our Master, we saw one casting out devils in thy name;  and we prevented him, because he followed not thee with us.

[26:16] Jesus said unto them, Prevent him not; for no man doeth powers in my name, and can hasten to speak evil ,  of me.

[26:17] Every one who is not in opposition to you is with you.

[26:18] Woe unto the world Arabic, p.

[26:19] because of trials! but woe unto that man by whose hand the trials come!  If thy hand or thy foot injure thee, cut it off, and cast it from thee; for it is better for thee to enter into life being halt or maimed, and not that thou shouldest have two hands or two feet, and fall into the hell of fire that burneth for ever; ,  where their worm dieth not, and their fire is not quenched.

[26:20] And if thine eye seduce  thee, pluck it out, and cast it from thee; for it is better for thee to enter the kingdom of God with one eye, than that thou shouldest have two eyes, and fall into the ,  fire of Gehenna; where their worm dieth not, and their fire is not quenched.

[26:21] Every  one shall be salted with fire, and every sacrifice shall be salted with salt.

[26:22] How good  is salt! but if the salt also be tasteless, wherewith shall it be salted? It is fit neither for the land nor for dung, but they cast it out.

[26:23] He that hath ears to hear, let him  hear.

[26:24] Have ye salt in yourselves, and be in peace one with another.

[26:25] And he arose from thence, and came to the borders of Judaea beyond Jordan: and there went unto him thither great multitudes, and he healed them; and he taught  them also, according to his custom.

[26:26] And the Pharisees came unto him, tempting  him, and asking him, Is it lawful for a man to put away his wife? He said, What  did Moses command you? They said, Moses made it allowable for us, saying, Whosoever  will, let him write a writing of divorcement, and put away his wife.

[26:27] Jesus answered and said unto them, Have ye not read, He that made them from the beginning  made them male and female, and said, For this reason shall the man leave his father Arabic, p.

[26:28] and his mother, and cleave to his wife; and they both shall be one body?  So then they are not twain, but one body; the thing, then, which God hath  joined together, let no man put asunder.

[26:29] And those Pharisees said unto him, Why did Moses consent that a man should give a writing of divorcement and put her away?  Jesus said unto them, Moses because of the hardness of your hearts gave you leave  to divorce your wives; but in the beginning it was not so.

[26:30] I say unto you, Whosoever putteth away his wife without fornication, and marrieth another, hath exposed  her to adultery.

[26:31] And his disciples, when he entered the house, asked him again  about that.

[26:32] And he said unto them, Every one who putteth away his wife, and  marrieth another, hath exposed her to adultery.

[26:33] And any woman that leaveth her husband, and becometh another's, hath committed adultery.

[26:34] And whosoever marrieth  her that is divorced hath committed adultery.

[26:35] And his disciples said unto him, If there be between the man and the woman such a case as this, it is not good for  a man to marry.

[26:36] He said unto them, Not every man can endure this saying, except  him to whom it is given.

[26:37] There are eunuchs which from their mother's womb were born so; and there are eunuchs which through men became eunuchs; and there are eunuchs which made themselves eunuchs for the sake of the kingdom of heaven.

[26:38] He that is able to be content, let him be content.

[26:39] Then they brought to him children, that he should lay his hand upon them, and  pray: and his disciples were rebuking those that were bringing them.

[26:40] And Jesus saw, and it was distressing to him; and he said unto them, Suffer the children to Arabic, p.

[26:41] come unto me, and prevent them not; for those that are like these have  the kingdom of God.

[26:42] Verily I say unto you, Whosoever receiveth not the  kingdom of God as this child, shall not enter it.

[26:43] And he took them in his arms, and laid his hand upon them, and blessed them.

[27:1] Section XXVI.

[27:2] ,  And there came unto him publicans and sinners to hear his word.

[27:3] And the scribes and the Pharisees murmured, and said, This man receiveth sinners, and  eateth with them.

[27:4] And Jesus, when he beheld their murmuring, spake unto them  this parable: What man of you, having an hundred sheep, if one of them were lost, would not leave the ninety-nine in the wilderness, and go and seek the straying one  till he found it? Verily I say unto you, When he findeth it, he will rejoice over it  more than over the ninety-nine that went not astray; and bear it on his shoulders, and bring it to his house, and call his friends and neighbours, and say unto them,  Rejoice with me, since I have found my straying sheep.

[27:5] So your Father which is in heaven willeth not that one of these little ones that have strayed should perish,  and he seeketh for them repentance.

[27:6] I say unto you, Thus there shall be rejoicing in heaven over one sinner that repenteth, more than over ninety-nine righteous persons that do not need repentance.

[27:7] And what woman having ten drachmas would lose one of them, and not light a  lamp, and sweep the house, and seek it with care till she found it; and when she found it, call her friends and neighbours, and say unto them, Rejoice with me, as I  have found my drachma that was lost? I say unto you, Thus there shall be joy Arabic, p.

[27:8] before the angels of God over the one sinner that repenteth, more than over the ninety-nine righteous persons that do not need repentance.

[27:9] ,  And Jesus spake unto them also another parable: A man had two sons: and the younger son said unto him, My father, give me my portion that belongeth to  me of thy goods.

[27:10] And he divided between them his property.

[27:11] And after a few days the younger son gathered everything that belonged to him, and went into a  far country, and there squandered his property by living prodigally.

[27:12] And when he had exhausted everything he had, there occurred a great dearth in that country.

[27:13] And when he was in want, he went and joined himself to one of the people of a city  of that country; and that man sent him into the field to feed the swine.

[27:14] And he used to long to fill his belly with the carob that those swine were eating: and no man  gave him.

[27:15] And when he returned unto himself, he said, How many hired servants now in my father's house have bread enough and to spare, while I here perish with  hunger! I will arise and go to my father's house, and say unto him, My father, I  have sinned in heaven and before thee, and am not worthy now to be called thy  son: make me as one of thy hired servants.

[27:16] And he arose, and came to his father.

[27:17] But his father saw him while he was at a distance, and was moved with compassion  for him, and ran, and fell on his breast, and kissed him.

[27:18] And his son said unto him, My father, I have sinned in heaven and before thee, and am not worthy to be  called thy son.

[27:19] His father said unto his servants, Bring forth a stately robe, and put  it on him; and put a ring on his hand, and put on him shoes on his feet: and bring and  slay a fatted ox, that we may eat and make merry: for this my son was dead, and is  Arabic, p.

[27:20] alive; and was lost, and is found.

[27:21] And they began to be merry.

[27:22] Now his elder son was in the field; and when he came and drew near to the house,  he heard the sound of many singing.

[27:23] And he called one of the lads, and asked him  what this was.

[27:24] He said unto him, Thy brother hath arrived; and thy father hath  slain a fatted ox, since he hath received him safe and sound.

[27:25] And he was angry,  and would not enter; so his father went out, and besought him to enter.

[27:26] And he said to his father, How many years do I serve thee in bondage, and I never transgressed a commandment of thine; and thou hast never given me a kid, that I might  make merry with my friends? but this thy son, when he had squandered thy  property with harlots, and come, thou hast slain for him a fatted ox.

[27:27] His father said unto him, My son, thou art at all times with me, and everything I have is  thine.

[27:28] It behoveth thee to rejoice and make merry, since this thy brother was dead, and is alive; and was lost, and is found.

[27:29] And he spake a parable unto his disciples: There was a rich man, and he had  a steward; and he was accused to him that he had squandered his property.

[27:30] So his lord called him, and said unto him, What is this that I hear regarding thee? Give me the account of thy stewardship; for it is now impossible that thou shouldest  be a steward for me.

[27:31] The steward said within himself, What shall I do, seeing that my lord taketh from me the stewardship? To dig I am not able; and to beg I  am ashamed.

[27:32] I know what I will do, that, when I go out of the stewardship, they  may receive me into their houses.

[27:33] And he called one after another of his lord's  debtors, and said to the first, How much owest thou my lord? He said unto him, An hundred portions of oil.

[27:34] He said unto him, Take thy writing, and sit down, and write  quickly fifty portions.

[27:35] And he said to the next, And thou, how much owest thou my lord? He said unto him, An hundred cors of wheat.

[27:36] He said unto him, Take  Arabic, p.

[27:37] thy writing, and sit down, and write eighty cors.

[27:38] And our lord commended the sinful steward because he had done a wise deed; for the children  of this world are wiser than the children of the light in this their age.

[27:39] And I also say unto you, Make unto yourselves friends with the wealth of this unrighteousness;  so that, when it is exhausted, they may receive you into their tents for ever.

[27:40] He who is faithful in a little is faithful also in much: and he who is unrighteous in a  little is unrighteous also in much.

[27:41] If then in the wealth of unrighteousness ye were  not trustworthy, who will intrust you with the truth? If ye are not found faithful in what does not belong to you, who will give you what belongeth to you?.

[28:1] Section XXVII.

[28:2] Therefore the kingdom of heaven is like a certain king, who would make a  reckoning with his servants.

[28:3] And when he began to make it, they brought to him one who  owed him ten talents.

[28:4] And because he had not wherewith to pay, his lord ordered that he should be sold, he, and his wife, and children, and all that he  had, and payment be made.

[28:5] So that servant fell down and worshipped him, and said unto him, My lord, have patience with me, and I shall pay thee everything.

[28:6] And the lord of that servant had compassion, and released him, and forgave him his  debt.

[28:7] And that servant went out, and found one of his fellow-servants, who owed him Arabic, p.

[28:8] a hundred pence; and he took him, and dealt severely with him, and said  unto him, Give me what thou owest.

[28:9] So the fellow-servant fell down at his  feet, and besought him, and said, Grant me respite, and I will pay thee.

[28:10] And he would not; but took him, and cast him into prison, till he should give him his debt.

[28:11] And when their fellow-servants saw what happened, it distressed them much; and  they came and told their lord of all that had taken place.

[28:12] Then his lord called him, and said unto him, Thou wicked servant, all that debt I forgave thee, because  thou besoughtest me: was it not then incumbent on thee also to have mercy on thy  fellow-servant, as I had mercy on thee? And his lord became wroth, and delivered  him to the scourgers, till he should pay all that he owed.

[28:13] So shall my Father which is in heaven do unto you, if one forgive not his brother his wrong conduct from  his heart.

[28:14] Take heed within yourselves: if thy brother sin, rebuke him; and if he  repent, forgive him.

[28:15] And if he act wrongly towards thee seven times in a day, and on that day return seven times unto thee, and say, I repent towards thee; forgive him.

[28:16] And if thy brother act wrongly towards thee, go and reprove him between thee and  him alone: if he hear thee, thou hast gained thy brother.

[28:17] But if he hear thee not, take with thee one or two, and so at the mouth of two or three every saying shall  be established.

[28:18] And if he listen not to these also, tell the congregation; and if he listen not even to the congregation, let him be unto thee as a publican and a Gentile.

[28:19] Verily I say unto you, All that ye bind on earth shall be bound in heaven:  and what ye loose on earth shall be loosed in heaven.

[28:20] I say unto you also, If two of you agree on earth to ask, everything shall be granted them from my Father  Arabic, p.

[28:21] which is in heaven.

[28:22] For where two or three are gathered in my name, there  am I amongst them.

[28:23] Then Cephas drew near to him, and said unto him, My Lord, how many times, if my brother act wrongly towards me, should I forgive him?  until seven times? Jesus said unto him, I say not unto thee, Until seven; but, Until seventy  times seven, seven.

[28:24] And the servant that knoweth his lord's will, and maketh not  ready for him according to his will, shall meet with much punishment; but he that knoweth not, and doeth something for which he meriteth punishment, shall meet with slight punishment.

[28:25] Every one to whom much hath been given, much shall be asked of him; and he that hath had much committed to him, much shall be  required at his hand.

[28:26] I came to cast fire upon the earth; and I would that it had  been kindled already.

[28:27] And I have a baptism to be baptized with, and greatly am  I straitened till it be accomplished.

[28:28] See that ye despise not one of these little ones that believe in me.

[28:29] Verily I say unto you, Their angels at all times see the  face of my Father which is in heaven.

[28:30] The Son of man came to save the thing which was lost.

[28:31] And after that, Jesus walked in Galilee; and he did not like to walk in Judaea,  because the Jews sought to kill him.

[28:32] And there came people who told him of  the Galilaeans, those whose blood Pilate had mingled with their sacrifices.

[28:33] Jesus answered and said unto them, Do ye imagine that those Galilaeans were sinners  more than all the Galilaeans, so that this thing has come upon them? Nay.

[28:34] Verily I say unto you now, that ye shall all also, if ye repent not, likewise perish.

[28:35] Or perchance those eighteen on whom the palace fell in Siloam, and slew them, do ye imagine that they were to be condemned more than all the people that dwell  Arabic, p.

[28:36] in Jerusalem? Nay.

[28:37] Verily I say unto you, If ye do not all repent, ye shall perish like them.

[28:38] And he spake unto them this parable: A man had a fig tree planted in his vineyard;  and he came and sought fruit thereon, and found none.

[28:39] So he said to the husbandman, Lo, three years do I come and seek fruit on this fig tree, and find  none: cut it down; why doth it render the ground unoccupied? The husbandman said unto him, My lord, leave it this year also, that I may dig about it, and dung  it; then if it bear fruit—! and if not, then cut it down in the coming year.

[28:40] And when Jesus was teaching on the sabbath day in one of the synagogues,  there was there a woman that had a spirit of disease eighteen years; and she was  bowed down, and could not straighten herself at all.

[28:41] And Jesus saw her, and called  her, and said unto her, Woman, be loosed from thy disease.

[28:42] And he put his hand  upon her; and immediately she was straightened, and praised God.

[28:43] And the chief of the synagogue answered with anger, because Jesus had healed on a sabbath, and said unto the multitudes, There are six days in which work ought to be done;  come in them and be healed, and not on the sabbath day.

[28:44] But Jesus answered and said unto him, Ye hypocrites, doth not each of you on the sabbath day loose  his ox or his ass from the manger, and go and water it? Ought not this woman, who is a daughter of Abraham, and whom the devil hath bound eighteen years,  to be loosed from this bond on the sabbath day? And when he said this, they were all put to shame, those standing, who were opposing him: and all the people were pleased with all the wonders that proceeded from his hand.

[29:1] Section XXVIII.

[29:2] ,  Arabic, p.

[29:3] And at that time the feast of tabernacles of the Jews drew near.

[29:4] So the brethren of Jesus said unto him, Remove now hence, and go to Judaea, that  thy disciples may see the deeds that thou doest.

[29:5] For no man doeth a thing secretly  and wisheth to be apparent.

[29:6] If thou doest this, shew thyself to the world.

[29:7] For  up to this time not even the brethren of Jesus believed on him.

[29:8] Jesus said unto them, My time till now has not arrived; but as for you, your time is alway ready.

[29:9] It is not possible for the world to hate you; but me it hateth, for I bear witness  against it, that its deeds are evil.

[29:10] As for you, go ye up unto this feast: but I go  not up now to this feast; for my time has not yet been completed.

[29:11] He said this, and remained behind in Galilee.

[29:12] But when his brethren went up unto the feast, he journeyed from Galilee, and  came to the borders of Judaea, to the country beyond Jordan; and there came after  him great multitudes, and he healed them all there.

[29:13] And he went out, and proceeded  to the feast, not openly, but as one that conceals himself.

[29:14] And the Jews sought him  at the feast, and said, In what place is this man? And there occurred much murmuring there in the great multitude that came to the feast, on his account.

[29:15] For  some said, He is good: and others said, Nay, but he leadeth the people astray.

[29:16] But no man spake of him openly for fear of the Jews.

[29:17] Arabic, p.

[29:18] But when the days of the feast of tabernacles were half over, Jesus went  up to the temple, and taught.

[29:19] And the Jews wondered, and said, How doth  this man know writing, seeing he hath not learned? Jesus answered and said, My doctrine  is not mine, but his that sent me.

[29:20] Whoever wisheth to do his will understandeth my doctrine, whether it be from God, or whether I speak of mine own accord.

[29:21] Whosoever speaketh of his own accord seeketh praise for himself; but whosoever seeketh praise for him that sent him, he is true, and unrighteousness in his heart  there is none.

[29:22] Did not Moses give you the law, and no man of you keepeth the  law? Why seek ye to kill me? The multitude answered and said unto him, Thou  hast demons: who seeketh to kill thee? Jesus answered and said unto them, I did  one deed, and ye all marvel because of this.

[29:23] Moses hath given you circumcision (not because it is from Moses, but it is from the fathers); and ye on the sabbath  circumcise a man.

[29:24] And if a man is circumcised on the sabbath day, that the law of Moses may not be broken; are ye angry at me, because I healed on the sabbath  day the whole man? Judge not with hypocrisy, but judge righteous judgement.

[29:25] And some people from Jerusalem said, Is not this he whom they seek to slay?  And lo, he discourseth with them openly, and they say nothing unto him.

[29:26] Think  you that our elders have learned that this is the Messiah indeed? But this man is known whence he is; and the Messiah, when he cometh, no man knoweth whence  he is.

[29:27] So Jesus lifted up his voice as he taught in the temple, and said, Ye both know me, and know whence I am; and of my own accord am I not come, but he  Arabic, p.

[29:28] that sent me is true, he whom ye know not: but I know him; for I am  from him, and he sent me.

[29:29] And they sought to seize him: and no man  laid a hand on him, because his hour had not yet come.

[29:30] But many of the multitude believed on him; and they said, The Messiah, when he cometh, can it be that he will do more than these signs that this man doeth?   And a man of that multitude said unto our Lord, Teacher, say to my brother  that he divide with me the inheritance.

[29:31] Jesus said unto him, Man, who is it that  appointed me over you as a judge and divider? And he said unto his disciples, Take heed within yourselves of all inordinate desire; for it is not in abundance of  possessions that life shall be.

[29:32] And he gave them this parable: The ground of a  rich man brought forth abundant produce: and he pondered within himself, and  said, What shall I do, since I have no place to store my produce? And he said, I will do this: I will pull down the buildings of my barns, and build them, and make  them greater; and store there all my wheat and my goods.

[29:33] And I will say to my soul, Soul, thou hast much goods laid by for many years; take thine ease, eat,  drink, enjoy thyself.

[29:34] God said unto him, O thou of little intelligence, this night shall thy soul be taken from thee; and this that thou hast prepared, whose shall it  be? So is he that layeth up treasures for himself, and is not rich in God.

[29:35] And while Jesus was going in the way, there came near to him a young man of the rulers, and fell on his knees, and asked him, and said, Good Teacher, what is  it that I must do that I may have eternal life? Jesus said unto him, Why callest thou  me good, while there is none good but the one, even God? Thou knowest the commandments.

[29:36] If thou wouldest enter into life, keep the commandments.

[29:37] The young Arabic, p.

[29:38] man said unto him, Which of the commandments? Jesus said unto him,  Thou shalt not commit adultery, Thou shalt not steal, Thou shalt not kill, Thou shalt not bear false witness, Thou shalt not do injury, Honour thy father  and thy mother: and, Love thy neighbour as thyself.

[29:39] That young man said unto  him, All these have I kept from my youth: what then is it that I lack? And Jesus  looked intently at him, and loved him, and said unto him, If thou wouldest be perfect, what thou lackest is one thing: go away and sell everything that thou hast, and give to the poor, and thou shalt have treasure in heaven: and take thy  cross, and follow me.

[29:40] And that young man frowned at this word, and went away  feeling sad; for he was very rich.

[29:41] And when Jesus saw his sadness, he looked towards his disciples, and said unto them, How hard it is for them that have possessions to enter the kingdom of God!.

[30:1] Section XXIX.

[30:2] Verily I say unto you, It is difficult for a rich man to enter the kingdom of  heaven.

[30:3] And I say unto you also, that it is easier for a camel to enter the eye of  a needle, than for a rich man to enter the kingdom of God.

[30:4] And the disciples were wondering at these sayings.

[30:5] And Jesus answered and said unto them again, My children, how hard it is for those that rely on their possessions to enter the  kingdom of God! And those that were listening wondered more, and said amongst  themselves, being agitated, Who, thinkest thou, can be saved? And Jesus looked at them intently, and said unto them, With men this is not possible, but with God it is:  Arabic, p.

[30:6] it is possible for God to do everything.

[30:7] Simon Cephas said unto him, Lo, we have left everything, and followed thee; what is it, thinkest thou, that we  shall have? Jesus said unto them, Verily I say unto you, Ye that have followed me, in the new world, when the Son of man shall sit on the throne of his glory, ye also  shall sit on twelve thrones, and shall judge the twelve tribes of Israel.

[30:8] Verily I say unto you, No man leaveth houses, or brothers, or sisters, or father, or mother, or wife, or children, or kinsfolk, or lands, because of the kingdom of God, or for  my sake, and the sake of my gospel, who shall not obtain many times as much in this  time, and in the world to come inherit eternal life: and now in this time, houses, and brothers, and sisters, and mothers, and children, and lands, with persecution;  and in the world to come everlasting life.

[30:9] Many that are first shall be last, and that are last shall be first.

[30:10] And when the Pharisees heard all this, because of their love for wealth they  scoffed at him.

[30:11] And Jesus knew what was in their hearts, and said unto them, Ye are they that justify yourselves before men; while God knows your hearts: the thing that is lofty with men is base before God.

[30:12] And he began to say, A certain man was rich, and wore silk and purple, and enjoyed  himself every day in splendour: and there was a poor man named Lazarus, and  he was cast down at the door of the rich man, afflicted with sores, and he longed to fill Arabic, p.

[30:13] his belly with the crumbs that fell from the table of that rich man; yea,  even the dogs used to come and lick his sores.

[30:14] And it happened that that poor man died, and the angels conveyed him into the bosom of Abraham: and the  rich man also died, and was buried.

[30:15] And while he was being tormented in Hades,  he lifted up his eyes from afar, and saw Abraham with Lazarus in his bosom.

[30:16] And he called with a loud voice, and said, My father Abraham, have mercy upon me, and send Lazarus to wet the tip of his finger with water, and moisten my tongue  for me; for, behold, I am burned in this flame.

[30:17] Abraham said unto him, My son, remember that thou receivedst thy good things in thy life, and Lazarus his afflictions:  but now, behold, he is at rest here, and thou art tormented.

[30:18] And in addition to all this, there is between us and you a great abyss placed, so that they that would cross unto you from hence cannot, nor yet from thence do they cross unto  us.

[30:19] He said unto him, Then I beseech thee, my father, to send him to my father's  house; for I have five brethren; let him go, that they also sin not, and come to  the abode of this torment.

[30:20] Abraham said unto him, They have Moses and the  prophets; let them hear them.

[30:21] He said unto him, Nay, my father Abraham: but  let a man from the dead go unto them, and they will repent.

[30:22] Abraham said unto him, If they listen neither to Moses nor to the prophets, neither if a man from the dead rose would they believe him.

[30:23] The kingdom of heaven is like a man that is a householder, which went out early  in the morning to hire labourers for his vineyard.

[30:24] And he agreed with the labourers on  one penny a day for each labourer, and he sent them into his vineyard.

[30:25] And he went  Arabic, p.

[30:26] out in three hours, and saw others standing in the market idle.

[30:27] He said unto them, Go ye also into my vineyard, and what is right I will pay you.

[30:28] And they went.

[30:29] And he went out also at the sixth and the ninth hour, and did likewise,  and sent them.

[30:30] And about the eleventh hour he went out, and found others standing idle.

[30:31] He said unto them, Why are ye standing the whole day idle?  They said unto him, Because no one hath hired us.

[30:32] He said unto them, Go ye  also into the vineyard, and what is right ye shall receive.

[30:33] So when evening came, the lord of the vineyard said unto his steward, Call the labourers, and pay them  their wages; and begin with the later ones, and end with the former ones.

[30:34] And  those of eleven hours came, and received each a penny.

[30:35] When therefore the first came, they supposed that they should receive something more; and they also  received each a penny.

[30:36] And when they received it, they spake angrily against the  householder, and said, These last worked one hour, and thou hast made them equal  with us, who have suffered the heat of the day, and its burden.

[30:37] He answered and said unto one of them, My friend, I do thee no wrong: was it not for a penny that  thou didst bargain with me? Take what is thine, and go thy way; for I wish to  give this last as I have given thee.

[30:38] Or am I not entitled to do with what is mine  what I choose? Or is thine eye perchance evil, because I am good? Thus shall the last ones be first, and the first last.

[30:39] The called are many, and the chosen are few.

[30:40] And when Jesus entered into the house of one of the chiefs of the Pharisees to eat bread on the sabbath day, and they were watching him to see what he would ,  do, and there was before him a man which had the dropsy, Jesus answered and  said unto the scribes and the Pharisees, Is it lawful on the sabbath to heal? But Arabic, p.

[30:41] they were silent.

[30:42] So he took him, and healed him, and sent him away.

[30:43] And he said unto them, Which of you shall have his son or his ox fall on the sabbath day into a well, and not lift him up straightway, and draw water for  him? And they were not able to answer him a word to that.

[31:1] Section XXX.

[31:2] And he spake a parable unto those which were bidden there, because he saw  them choose the places that were in the highest part of the sitting room: When a man invites thee to a feast, do not go and sit at the head of the room; lest there  be there a man more honourable than thou, and he that invited you come and say unto thee, Give the place to this man: and thou be ashamed when thou risest and  takest another place.

[31:3] But when thou art invited, go and sit last; so that when he that invited thee cometh, he may say unto thee, My friend, go up higher: and  thou shalt have praise before all that were invited with thee.

[31:4] For every one that exalteth himself shall be abased; and every one that abaseth himself shall be exalted.

[31:5] And he said also to him that had invited him, When thou makest a feast or a banquet, do not invite thy friends, nor even thy brethren, nor thy kinsmen, nor thy  rich neighbours; lest haply they also invite thee, and thou have this reward.

[31:6] But when thou makest a feast, invite the poor, and those with withered hand, and the  lame, and the blind: and blessed art thou, since they have not the means to reward  thee; that thy reward may be at the rising of the righteous.

[31:7] And when one of them that were invited heard that, he said unto him, Blessed is he that shall eat bread in the kingdom of God.

[31:8] ,  Jesus answered again in parables, and said, The kingdom of heaven hath been likened Arabic, p.

[31:9] to a certain king, which made a feast for his son, and prepared a  great banquet, and invited many: and he sent his servants at the time of the feast to inform them that were invited, Everything is made ready for you; come.

[31:10] And  they would not come, but began all of them with one voice to make excuse.

[31:11] And the first said unto them, Say to him, I have bought a field, and I must needs go out  to see it: I pray thee to release me, for I ask to be excused.

[31:12] And another said, I have bought five yoke of oxen, and I am going to examine them: I pray thee  to release me, for I ask to be excused.

[31:13] And another said, I have married a wife,  and therefore I cannot come.

[31:14] And the king sent also other servants, and said, Say to those that were invited, that my feast is ready, and my oxen and my fatlings are  slain, and everything is ready: come to the feast.

[31:15] But they made light of it, and  went, one to his field, and another to his merchandise: and the rest took his  servants, and entreated them shamefully, and killed them.

[31:16] And one of the servants  came, and informed his lord of what had happened.

[31:17] And when the king heard, he became angry, and sent his armies; and they destroyed those murderers, and  burned their cities.

[31:18] Then he said to his servants, The feast is prepared, but those  that were invited were not worthy.

[31:19] Go out quickly into the markets and into the partings of the ways of the city, and bring in hither the poor, and those with pains, and the lame, and the blind.

[31:20] And the servants did as the king commanded them.

[31:21] And they came, and said unto him, Our lord, we have done all that thou commandedst  us, and there is here still room.

[31:22] So the lord said unto his servants, Go out into the roads, and the ways, and the paths, and every one that ye find, invite  Arabic, p.

[31:23] to the feast, and constrain them to enter, till my house is filled.

[31:24] I say unto you, that no one of those people that were invited shall taste of my feast.

[31:25] And those servants went out into the roads, and gathered all that they found, good and  bad: and the banquet-house was filled with guests.

[31:26] And the king entered to see those  who were seated, and he saw there a man not wearing a festive garment: and he said unto him, My friend, how didst thou come in here not having on festive garments?  And he was silent.

[31:27] Then the king said to the servants, Bind his hands and his feet, and put him forth into the outer darkness; there shall be weeping and  gnashing of teeth.

[31:28] The called are many; and the chosen, few.

[31:29] And after that, the time of the feast of unleavened bread of the Jews arrived,  and Jesus went out to go to Jerusalem.

[31:30] And as he went in the way, there met him  ten persons who were lepers, and stood afar off: and they lifted up their voice, and  said, Our Master, Jesus, have mercy upon us.

[31:31] And when he saw them, he said unto them, Go and shew yourselves unto the priests.

[31:32] And when they went, they  were cleansed.

[31:33] And one of them, when he saw himself cleansed, returned, and  was praising God with a loud voice; and he fell on his face before the feet of  Jesus, giving him thanks: and this man was a Samaritan.

[31:34] Jesus answered and said,  Were not those that were cleansed ten? where then are the nine? Not one of them turned aside to come and praise God, but this man who is of a strange  people.

[31:35] He said unto him, Arise, and go thy way; for thy faith hath given thee life.

[31:36] And while they were going up in the way to Jerusalem, Jesus went in front of them; and they wondered, and followed him fearing.

[31:37] And he took his twelve disciples apart,  and began to tell them privately what was about to befall him.

[31:38] And he said unto Arabic, p.

[31:39] them, We are going up to Jerusalem, and all the things shall be fulfilled  that are written in the prophets concerning the Son of man.

[31:40] He shall be delivered to the chief priests and the scribes; and they shall condemn him to death,  and deliver him to the peoples; and they shall treat him shamefully, and scourge  him, and spit in his face, and humble him,and crucify him, and slay him: and on  the third day he shall rise.

[31:41] But they understood not one thing of this; but this word was hidden from them, and they did not perceive these things that were addressed to them.

[31:42] Then came near to him the mother of the (two) sons of Zebedee, she and her (two) sons, and worshipped him, and asked of him a certain thing.

[31:43] And he said  unto her, What wouldest thou? And James and John, her two sons, came forward, and said unto him, Teacher, we would that all that we ask thou wouldest  do unto us.

[31:44] He said unto them, What would ye that I should do unto you?  They said unto him, Grant us that we may sit, the one on thy right, and the other  on thy left, in thy kingdom and thy glory.

[31:45] And Jesus said unto them, Ye know not what ye ask.

[31:46] Are ye able to drink the cup that I am to drink? and with the  baptism that I am to be baptized with, will ye be baptized? And they said unto him, We are able.

[31:47] Jesus said unto them, The cup that I drink ye shall drink; and  with the baptism wherewith I am baptized ye shall be baptized: but that ye should sit on my right and on my left is not mine to give; but it is for him for whom my Father hath prepared it.

[32:1] Section XXXI.

[32:2] And when the ten heard, they were moved with anger against James and John.

[32:3] And Jesus called them, and said unto them, Ye know that the rulers of the nations  are their lords; and their great men are set in authority over them.

[32:4] Not thus shall it Arabic, p.

[32:5] be amongst you: but he amongst you that would be great, let him be to you a  servant; and whoever of you would be first, let him be to every man a  bond-servant: even as the Son of man also came not to be served, but to serve, and  to give himself a ransom in place of the many.

[32:6] He said this, and was going about  the villages and the cities, and teaching; and he went to Jerusalem.

[32:7] And a man asked him, Are those that shall be saved few? Jesus answered and said unto  them, Strive ye to enter at the narrow door: I say unto you now, that many shall  seek to enter, and shall not be able—from the time when the master of the house riseth, and closeth the door, and ye shall be standing without, and shall knock at the door, and shall begin to say, Our lord, open unto us; and he shall answer and  say, I say unto you, I know you not whence ye are: and ye shall begin to say,  Before thee we did eat and drink, and in our markets didst thou teach; and he shall say unto you, I know you not whence ye are; depart from me, ye servants  of untruth.

[32:8] There shall be weeping and gnashing of teeth, when ye see Abraham, and Isaac, and Jacob, and all the prophets, in the kingdom of God, while ye are  put forth without.

[32:9] And they shall come from the east and the west, and from the  north and the south, and shall sit down in the kingdom of God.

[32:10] And there shall then be last that have become first, and first that have become last.

[32:11] ,  And when Jesus entered and passed through Jericho, there was a man named Zacchaeus,  rich, and chief of the publicans.

[32:12] And he desired to see Jesus who he was; and he was not able for the pressure of the crowd, because Zacchaeus was little of stature.

[32:13] Arabic, p.

[32:14] And he hastened, and went before Jesus, and went up into an unripe fig  tree to see Jesus: for he was to pass thus.

[32:15] And when Jesus came to that place, he saw him, and said unto him, Make haste, and come down, Zacchaeus:  to-day I must be in thy house.

[32:16] And he hastened, and came down, and received  him joyfully.

[32:17] And when they all saw, they murmured, and said, He hath gone in  and lodged with a man that is a sinner.

[32:18] So Zacchaeus stood, and said unto Jesus, My Lord, now half of my possessions I give to the poor, and what I have unjustly  taken from every man I give him fourfold.

[32:19] Jesus said unto him, Today is salvation  come to this house, because this man also is a son of Abraham.

[32:20] For the Son of man came to seek and save the thing that was lost.

[32:21] And when Jesus went out of Jericho, he and his disciples, there came after him  a great multitude.

[32:22] And there was a blind man sitting by the way side begging.

[32:23] And his name was Timaeus, the son of Timaeus.

[32:24] And he heard the sound of the  multitude passing, and asked, Who is this? They said unto him, Jesus the Nazarene  passeth by.

[32:25] And when he heard that it was Jesus, he called out with a loud  voice, and said, Jesus, son of David, have mercy on me.

[32:26] And those that went before Jesus were rebuking him, that he should hold his peace: but he cried the  more, and said, Son of David, have mercy on me.

[32:27] And Jesus stood, and commanded that they should call him.

[32:28] And they called the blind man, and said unto  him, Be of good courage, and rise; for, behold, he calleth thee.

[32:29] And the blind  man threw away his garment, and rose, and came to Jesus.

[32:30] Jesus said unto him, What dost thou wish that I should do unto thee? And that blind man said unto him, My Lord and Master, that my eyes may be opened, so that I may see thee.

[32:31] Arabic, p.

[32:32] And Jesus had compassion on him, and touched his eyes, and said unto  him, See; for thy faith hath saved thee.

[32:33] And immediately he received his sight, and came after him, and praised God; and all the people that saw praised God.

[32:34] And he spake a parable because he was nearing Jerusalem, and they supposed  that at that time the kingdom of God was about to appear.

[32:35] He said unto them, A man, a son of a great race, went into a far country, to receive a kingdom, and  return.

[32:36] And he called his ten servants, and gave them ten shares, and said unto  them, Trade till the time of my coming.

[32:37] But the people of his city hated him, and  sent messengers after him, and said, We will not that this man reign over us.

[32:38] And when he had received a kingdom, and returned, he said that the servants to whom he had given the money should be called unto him, that he might know what each  of them had traded.

[32:39] And the first came, and said, My lord, thy share hath gained  ten shares.

[32:40] The king said unto him, Thou good and faithful servant, who hast  been found faithful in a little, be thou set over ten districts.

[32:41] And the second came,  and said, My lord, thy portion hath gained five portions.

[32:42] And he said unto him  also, And thou shalt be set over five districts.

[32:43] And another came, and said, My  lord, here is thy portion, which was with me laid by in a napkin: I feared thee, because thou art a hard man, and takest what thou didst not leave, and seekest  what thou didst not give, and reapest what thou didst not sow.

[32:44] His lord said unto him, From thy mouth shall I judge thee, thou wicked and idle servant, who wast untrustworthy.

[32:45] Thou knewest that I am a hard man, and take what I did not  leave, and reap what I did not sow: why didst thou not put my money at usury,  and so I might come and seek it, with its gains? And he said unto those that were standing in front of him, Take from him the share, and give it to him that hath ,  Arabic, p.

[32:46] ten shares.

[32:47] They said unto him, Our lord, he hath ten shares.

[32:48] He said unto them, I say unto you, Every one that hath shall be given unto; and  he that hath not, that which he hath also shall be taken from him.

[32:49] And those mine enemies who would not that I should reign over them, bring them, and slay them before me.

[33:1] Section XXXII.

[33:2] And when Jesus entered Jerusalem, he went up to the temple of God, and found  there oxen and sheep and doves.

[33:3] And when he beheld those that sold and those that bought, and the money-changers sitting, he made for himself a scourge of rope, and drove them all out of the temple, and the sheep and the oxen, and the money-changers; and he threw down their money, and upset their tables, and the seats of  them that sold the doves; and he was teaching, and saying unto them, Is it not written, My house is a house of prayer for all peoples? and ye have made it a den  for robbers.

[33:4] And he said unto those that sold the doves, Take this hence, and  make not my Father's house a house of merchandise.

[33:5] And he suffered not any  one to carry vessels inside the temple.

[33:6] And his disciples remembered the scripture,  The zeal of thy house hath eaten me up.

[33:7] The Jews answered and said unto him,  What sign hast thou shewn us, that thou doest this? Jesus answered and said unto  them, Destroy this temple, and I shall raise it in three days.

[33:8] The Jews said unto him, This temple was built in forty-six years, and wilt thou raise it in three days?  But he spake unto them of the temple of his body, that when they destroyed it, he  Arabic, p.

[33:9] would raise it in three days.

[33:10] When therefore he rose from among the dead, his disciples remembered that he said this; and they believed the scriptures, and the word that Jesus spake.

[33:11] And when Jesus sat down over against the treasury, he observed how the multitudes were casting their offerings into the treasury: and many rich men were ,  throwing in much.

[33:12] And there came a poor widow, and cast in two mites.

[33:13] And Jesus called his disciples, and said unto them, Verily I say unto you, This poor  widow cast into the treasury more than all the people: and all of these cast into the place of the offering of God of the superfluity of their wealth; while this woman of her want threw in all that she possessed.

[33:14] And he spake unto them this parable, concerning people who trusted in themselves  that they are righteous, and despised every man: Two men went up to the  temple to pray; one of them a Pharisee, and the other a publican.

[33:15] And the Pharisee stood apart, and prayed thus, O Lord, I thank thee, since I am not like the rest of men, the unjust, the profligate, the extortioners, or even like this publican;  but I fast two days a week, and tithe all my possessions.

[33:16] And the publican was  standing at a distance, and he would not even lift up his eyes to heaven, but was  beating upon his breast, and saying, O Lord, have mercy on me, me the sinner.

[33:17] I say unto you, that this man went down justified to his house more than the Pharisee.

[33:18] Every one that exalteth himself shall be abased; and every one that abaseth himself shall be exalted.

[33:19] Arabic, p.

[33:20] And when eventide was come, he left all the people, and went outside the  city to Bethany, he and his twelve, and he remained there.

[33:21] And all the people, because they knew the place, came to him, and he received them; and them that  had need of healing he healed.

[33:22] And on the morning of the next day, when he returned  to the city from Bethany, he hungered.

[33:23] And he saw a fig tree at a distance on the beaten highway, having on it leaves.

[33:24] And he came unto it, expecting to find something on it; and when he came, he found nothing on it but the leaves—it was not  the season of figs—and he said unto it, Henceforward for ever let no man eat fruit of thee.

[33:25] And his disciples heard.

[33:26] And they came to Jerusalem.

[33:27] And there was there a man of the Pharisees,  named Nicodemus, ruler of the Jews.

[33:28] This man came unto Jesus by night, and said unto him, My Master, we know that thou hast been sent from God as a teacher; and no man can do these signs that thou doest, except him whom God is  with.

[33:29] Jesus answered and said unto him, Verily, verily, I say unto thee, If a man  be not born a second time, he cannot see the kingdom of God.

[33:30] Nicodemus said unto him, How can a man who is old be born? can he, think you, return again to  his mother's womb a second time, to enter and be born? Jesus answered and said unto him, Verily, verily, I say unto thee, If a man be not born of water and the Spirit,  he cannot enter the kingdom of God.

[33:31] For he that is born of flesh is flesh; and he that  is born of Spirit is spirit.

[33:32] Wonder not that I said unto thee that ye must be born a  Arabic, p.

[33:33] second time.

[33:34] The wind bloweth where it listeth, and thou hearest its voice, but thou knowest not from what place it cometh, nor whither it goeth: so  is every man that is born of the Spirit.

[33:35] Nicodemus answered and said unto him,  How can that be? Jesus answered and said unto him, Art thou teaching Israel,  and yet knowest not these things? Verily, verily, I say unto thee, What we know  we say, and what we have seen we witness: and ye receive not our witness.

[33:36] If I said unto you what is on earth, and ye believed not, how then, if I say unto you  what is in heaven, will ye believe? And no man hath ascended up into heaven, except him that descended from heaven, the Son of man, which is in heaven.

[33:37] And as Moses lifted up the serpent in the wilderness, so is the Son of man to be  lifted up; so that every man who may believe in him may not perish, but have  eternal life.

[33:38] God so loved the world, that he should give his only Son; and so every one that believeth on him should not perish, but should have eternal life.

[33:39] God sent not his Son into the world to judge the world; but that the world might  be saved by his hand.

[33:40] He that believeth in him shall not be judged: but he that believeth not is condemned beforehand, because he hath not believed in the name  of the only Son, the Son of God.

[33:41] This is the judgement, that the light came into the world, and men loved the darkness more than the light; because their deeds  were evil.

[33:42] Whosoever doeth evil deeds hateth the light, and cometh not to the  light, lest his deeds be reproved.

[33:43] But he that doeth the truth cometh to the light, that his deeds may be known, that they have been done in God.

[34:1] Section XXXIII.

[34:2] Arabic, p.

[34:3] And when evening came, Jesus went forth outside of the city, he and his  disciples.

[34:4] And as they passed in the morning, the disciples saw that fig tree  withered away from its root.

[34:5] And they passed by, and said, How did the fig tree dry  up immediately? And Simon remembered, and said unto him, My Master, behold,  that fig tree which thou didst curse hath dried up.

[34:6] And Jesus answered and said  unto them, Let there be in you the faith of God.

[34:7] Verily I say unto you, if ye believe, and doubt not in your hearts, and assure yourselves that that will be which  ye say, ye shall have what ye say.

[34:8] And if ye say to this mountain, Remove, and  fall into the sea, it shall be.

[34:9] And all that ye ask God in prayer, and believe, he ,  will give you.

[34:10] And the apostles said unto our Lord, Increase our faith.

[34:11] He said unto them, If there be in you faith like a grain of mustard, ye shall say to this fig tree, Be thou torn up, and be thou planted in the sea; and it will obey you.

[34:12] Who of you hath a servant driving a yoke of oxen or tending sheep, and if he  come from the field, will say unto him straightway, Go and sit down? Nay, he will say unto him, Make ready for me wherewith I may sup, and gird thy waist, and serve me, till I eat and drink; and afterwards thou shalt eat and drink also.

[34:13] Doth that servant haply, who did what he was bid, receive his praise? I think  not.

[34:14] So ye also, when ye have done all that ye were bid, say, We are idle servants; what it was our duty to do, we have done.

[34:15] For this reason I say unto you, Whatever ye pray and ask, believe that ye  Arabic, p.

[34:16] receive, and ye shall have.

[34:17] And when ye stand to pray, forgive what is in your heart against any man; and your Father which is in heaven will  forgive you also your wrong-doings.

[34:18] But if ye forgive not men their wrong-doings, neither will your Father forgive you also your wrong-doings.

[34:19] And he spake unto them a parable also, that they should pray at all times, and  not be slothful: There was a judge in a city, who feared not God, nor was ashamed  for men: and there was a widow in that city; and she came unto him, and said,  Avenge me of mine adversary.

[34:20] And he would not for a long time: but afterwards he said within himself, If of God I have no fear, and before men I have no shame;  yet because this widow vexeth me, I will avenge her, that she come not at all times ,  and annoy me.

[34:21] And our Lord said, Hear ye what the judge of injustice said.

[34:22] And shall not God still more do vengeance for his elect, who call upon him in the night  and in the day, and grant them respite? I say unto you, He will do vengeance for them speedily.

[34:23] Thinkest thou the Son of man will come and find faith on the earth?  ,  And they came again to Jerusalem.

[34:24] And it came to pass, on one of the days, as Jesus was walking in the temple, and teaching the people, and preaching the  gospel, that the chief priests and the scribes with the elders came upon him, and said unto him, Tell us: By what power doest thou this? and who gave thee this  power to do that? And Jesus said unto them, I also will ask you one word, and if  ye tell me, I also shall tell you by what power I do that.

[34:25] The baptism of John, from  what place is it? from heaven or of men? Tell me.

[34:26] And they reflected within themselves, Arabic, p.

[34:27] and said, If we shall say unto him, From heaven; he will say unto  us, For what reason did ye not believe him? But if we shall say, Of men;  we fear that the people will stone us, all of them.

[34:28] And all of them were holding  to John, that he was a true prophet.

[34:29] They answered and said unto him, We know  not.

[34:30] Jesus said unto them, Neither tell I you also by what power I work.

[34:31] What think ye? A man had two sons; and he went to the first, and said unto him, My  son, go to-day, and till in the vineyard.

[34:32] And he answered and said, I do not wish  to: but finally he repented, and went.

[34:33] And he went to the other, and said unto  him likewise.

[34:34] And he answered and said, Yea, my lord: and went not.

[34:35] Which of these two did the will of his father? They said unto him, The first.

[34:36] Jesus said unto them, Verily I say unto you, The publicans and harlots go before you into  the kingdom of God.

[34:37] John came unto you in the way of righteousness, and ye believed him not; but the publicans and harlots believed him; and ye, not even when ye saw, did ye repent at last, that ye might believe in him.

[34:38] Hear another parable: A man was a householder, and planted a vineyard, and surrounded it with a hedge, and digged in it a winepress, and built in it a tower, ,  and gave it to husbandmen, and went to a distance for a long time.

[34:39] So when the time of the fruits came, he sent his servants unto the husbandmen, that they might  send him of the produce of his vineyard.

[34:40] And those husbandmen beat him, and  sent him away empty.

[34:41] And he sent unto them another servant also; and they  stoned him, and wounded him, and sent him away with shameful handling.

[34:42] And he sent again another; and they slew him.

[34:43] And he sent many other servants unto  them.

[34:44] And the husbandmen took his servants, and one they beat, and another they  stoned, and another they slew.

[34:45] So he sent again other servants more than the first; and  Arabic, p.

[34:46] they did likewise with them.

[34:47] So the owner of the vineyard said, What shall I do? I will send my beloved son: it may be they will see him and be ,  ashamed.

[34:48] So at last he sent unto them his beloved son that he had.

[34:49] But the husbandmen, when they saw the son, said amongst themselves, This is the heir.

[34:50] ,  And they said, We will slay him, and so the inheritance will be ours.

[34:51] So they took  him, and put him forth without the vineyard, and slew him.

[34:52] When then the lord  of the vineyard shall come, what will he do with those husbandmen? They said unto him, He will destroy them in the worst of ways, and give the vineyard to  other husbandmen, who will give him fruit in its season.

[34:53] Jesus said unto them, Have ye never read in the scripture,  The stone which the builders declared to be base,  The same came to be at the head of the corner:   From God was this,  And it is wonderful in our eyes?   Therefore I say unto you, The kingdom of God shall be taken from you, and  given to a people that will produce fruit.

[34:54] And whosoever falleth on this stone shall be broken in pieces: but on whomsoever it falleth, it will grind him to  powder.

[34:55] And when the chief priests and the Pharisees heard his parables, they  perceived that it was concerning them he spake.

[34:56] And they sought to seize him; and they feared the multitude, because they were holding to him as the prophet.

[35:1] Section XXXIV.

[35:2] Then went the Pharisees and considered how they might ensnare him in a word,  and deliver him into the power of the judge, and into the power of the ruler.

[35:3] And they sent unto him their disciples, with the kinsfolk of Herod; and they said unto him, Arabic, p.

[35:4] Teacher, we know that thou speakest the truth, and teachest the way of God with equity, and art not lifted up by any man: for thou actest not so as to  be seen of any man.

[35:5] Tell us now, What is thy opinion? Is it lawful that we should  pay the tribute to Caesar, or not? shall we give, or shall we not give? But Jesus knew  their deceit, and said unto them, Why tempt ye me, ye hypocrites? Shew me the  penny of the tribute.

[35:6] So they brought unto him a penny.

[35:7] Jesus said unto them, To whom belongeth this image and inscription? They said unto him, To Caesar.

[35:8] ,  He said unto them, Give what is Caesar's to Caesar, and what is God's to God.

[35:9] And they could not make him slip in a single word before the people; and they marvelled at his word, and refrained.

[35:10] And on that day came the Sadducees, and said unto him, There is no life for  the dead.

[35:11] And they asked him, and said unto him, Teacher, Moses said unto us, If a man die, not having children, let his brother take his wife, and raise up seed  for his brother.

[35:12] Now there were with us seven brethren: and the first took a wife,  and died without children; and the second took his wife, and died without children;  and the third also took her; and in like manner the seven of them also, and they ,  died without leaving children.

[35:13] And last of them all the woman died also.

[35:14] At the resurrection, then, which of these seven shall have this woman? for all of them took  her.

[35:15] Jesus answered and said unto them, Is it not for this that ye have erred,  because ye know not the scriptures, nor the power of God? And the sons of this  world take wives, and the women become the men's; but those that have become worthy of that world, and the resurrection from among the dead, do not take  Arabic, p.

[35:16] wives, and the women also do not become the men's.

[35:17] Nor is it possible that they should die; but they are like the angels, and are the children of  God, because they have become the children of the resurrection.

[35:18] For in the resurrection of the dead, have ye not read in the book of Moses, how from the bush God said unto him, I am the God of Abraham, and the God of Isaac, and the God of Jacob?  And God is not the God of the dead, but of the living: for all of them are alive with him.

[35:19] And ye have erred greatly.

[35:20] ,  And when the multitudes heard, they were wondering at his teaching.

[35:21] And  some of the scribes answered and said unto him, Teacher, thou hast well said.

[35:22] But the rest of the Pharisees, when they saw his silencing the Sadducees on this point, gathered against him to contend with him.

[35:23] And one of the scribes, of those that knew the law, when he saw the excellence  of his answer to them, desired to try him, and said unto him, What shall I do to inherit eternal life? and, Which of the commandments is greater, and has precedence  in the law? Jesus said unto him, The first of all the commandments is, Hear, O  Israel; The Lord our God, the Lord is one: and thou shalt love the Lord thy God with all thy heart, and with all thy soul, and with all thy thought, and with all thy ,  strength.

[35:24] This is the great and preëminent commandment.

[35:25] And the second, which is like it, is, Thou shalt love thy neighbour as thyself.

[35:26] And another commandment  greater than these two there is not.

[35:27] On these two commandments, then, are hung the  Arabic, p.

[35:28] law and the prophets.

[35:29] That scribe said unto him, Excellent! my Master; thou hast said truly that he is one, and there is no other outside of him:  and that a man should love him with all his heart, and with all his thought, and with all his soul, and with all his strength, and that he should love his neighbour as  himself, is better than all savours and sacrifices.

[35:30] And Jesus saw him that he had answered wisely; and he answered and said unto him, Thou art not far from the ,  kingdom of God.

[35:31] Thou hast spoken rightly: do this, and thou shalt live.

[35:32] And he, as his desire was to justify himself, said unto him, And who is my neighbour?  Jesus said unto him, A man went down from Jerusalem to Jericho; and the robbers fell upon him, and stripped him, and beat him, his life remaining in him but little,  and went away.

[35:33] And it happened that there came down a certain priest that way;  and he saw him, and passed by.

[35:34] And likewise a Levite also came and reached  that place, and saw him, and passed by.

[35:35] And a certain Samaritan, as he journeyed,  came to the place where he was, and saw him, and had compassion on him, and came near, and bound up his strokes, and poured on them wine and oil; and he set him on the ass, and brought him to the inn, and expended his care upon him.

[35:36] And on the morrow of that day he took out two pence, and gave them to the innkeeper, and said unto him, Care for him; and if thou spendest upon him more,  when I return, I shall give thee.

[35:37] Who of these three now, thinkest thou, is nearest  to him that fell among the robbers? And he said unto him, He that had compassion  Arabic, p.

[35:38] on him.

[35:39] Jesus said unto him, Go, and do thou also likewise.

[35:40] And no man dared afterwards to ask him anything.

[35:41] And he was teaching every day in the temple.

[35:42] But the chief priests and scribes and the elders of the people sought to destroy him: and they could not find what  they should do with him; and all the people were hanging upon him to hear him.

[35:43] And many of the multitude believed on him, and said, The Messiah, when he  cometh, can it be that he will do more than these signs that this man doeth? And the Pharisees heard the multitudes say that of him; and the chief priests sent  officers to seize him.

[35:44] And Jesus said unto them, I am with you but a short time  yet, and I go to him that sent me.

[35:45] And ye shall seek me, and shall not find me:  and where I shall be, ye shall not be able to come.

[35:46] The Jews said within themselves, Whither hath this man determined to go that we shall not be able to find him? can it be that he is determined to go to the regions of the nations, and teach  the heathen? What is this word that he said, Ye shall seek me, and shall not find me: and where I am, ye cannot come?.

[36:1] Section XXXV.

[36:2] And on the great day, which is the last of the feast, Jesus stood, crying out and  saying, If any man is thirsty, let him come unto me, and drink.

[36:3] Every one that believeth in me, as the scriptures said, there shall flow from his belly rivers of pure  water.

[36:4] He said that referring to the Spirit, which those who believed in him were to receive: for the Spirit was not yet granted; and because Jesus had not yet been  Arabic, p.

[36:5] glorified.

[36:6] And many of the multitude that heard his words said, This is  in truth the prophet.

[36:7] And others said, This is the Messiah.

[36:8] But others  said, Can it be that the Messiah will come from Galilee? Hath not the scripture said that from the seed of David, and from Bethlehem, the village of David, the  Messiah cometh? And there occurred a dissension in the multitude because of him.

[36:9] And some of them were wishing to seize him; but no man laid a hand upon him.

[36:10] And those officers came to the chief priests and Pharisees: and the priests said  unto them, Why did ye not bring him? The officers said, Never spake man thus  as speaketh this man.

[36:11] The Pharisees said unto them, Perhaps ye also have gone ,  astray? Hath any of the rulers or the Pharisees haply believed in him? except  this people which knows not the law; they are accursed.

[36:12] Nicodemus, one of them,  he that had come to Jesus by night, said unto them, Doth our law haply condemn  a man, except it hear him first and know what he hath done? They answered and said unto him, Art thou also haply from Galilee? Search, and see that a prophet riseth not from Galilee.

[36:13] ,  And when the Pharisees assembled, Jesus asked them, and said, What say ye of  the Messiah? whose son is he? They said unto him, The son of David.

[36:14] He said unto them, And how doth David in the Holy Spirit call him Lord? for he said,   The Lord said unto my Lord,  Sit on my right hand,  That I may put thine enemies under thy feet.

[36:15] ,  If then David calleth him Lord, how is he his son? And no one was able to answer him; and no man dared from that day again to ask him of anything.

[36:16] And Jesus addressed them again, and said, I am the light of the world; and he that  followeth me shall not walk in darkness, but shall find the light of life.

[36:17] The Pharisees Arabic, p.

[36:18] said unto him, Thou bearest witness to thyself; thy witness is not true.

[36:19] Jesus  answered and said unto them, If I bear witness to myself, my witness is true; for I know whence I came, and whither I go; but ye know not whence I came, or ,  whither I go.

[36:20] And ye judge after the flesh; and I judge no man.

[36:21] And even if I judge, my judgement is true; because I am not alone, but I and my Father which ,  sent me.

[36:22] And in your law it is written, that the witness of two men is true.

[36:23] I am he that beareth witness to myself, and my Father which sent me beareth witness to  me.

[36:24] They said unto him, Where is thy Father? Jesus answered and said unto them, Ye know not me, nor my Father: for did ye know me, ye would know my  Father.

[36:25] He said these sayings in the treasury, where he was teaching in the  temple: and no man seized him; because his hour had not yet come.

[36:26] Jesus said unto them again, I go truly, and ye shall seek me and not find me, and ye shall die  in your sins: and where I go, ye cannot come.

[36:27] The Jews said, Will he haply kill  himself, that he saith, Where I go, ye cannot come? He said unto them, Ye are from below; and I am from above: ye are of this world; and I am not of this  world.

[36:28] I said unto you, that ye shall die in your sins: if ye believe not that I am  he, ye shall die in your sins.

[36:29] The Jews said, And thou, who art thou? Jesus said  unto them, If I should begin to speak unto you, I have concerning you many words and judgement: but he that sent me is true; and I, what I heard from him is what ,  I say in the world.

[36:30] And they knew not that he meant by that the Father.

[36:31] Jesus Arabic, p.

[36:32] said unto them again, When ye have lifted up the Son of man, then ye shall know that I am he: and I do nothing of myself, but as my Father  taught me, so I speak.

[36:33] And he that sent me is with me; and my Father hath not  left me alone; because I do what is pleasing to him at all times.

[36:34] And while he was saying that, many believed in him.

[36:35] And Jesus said to those Jews that believed in him, If ye abide in my words, truly  ye are my disciples; and ye shall know the truth, and the truth shall make you free.

[36:36] They said unto him, We are the seed of Abraham, and have never served any man  in the way of slavery: how then sayest thou, Ye shall be free children? Jesus said unto them, Verily, verily, I say unto you, Every one that doeth a sin is a slave of  sin.

[36:37] And the slave doth not remain for ever in the house; but the son remaineth ,  for ever.

[36:38] And if the Son set you free, truly ye shall be free children.

[36:39] I know that ye are the seed of Abraham; but ye seek to slay me, because ye are unable for my  word.

[36:40] And what I saw with my Father, I say: and what ye saw with your father,  ye do.

[36:41] They answered and said unto him, Our father is Abraham.

[36:42] Jesus said unto them, If ye were the children of Abraham, ye would do the deeds of Abraham.

[36:43] Now, behold, ye seek to kill me, a man that speak with you the truth, that I  heard from God: this did Abraham not do.

[36:44] And ye do the deeds of your father.

[36:45] They said unto him, We were not born of fornication; we have one Father, who is  God.

[36:46] Jesus said unto them, If God were your Father, ye would love me: I proceeded and came from God; and it was not of my own self that I came, but he sent  Arabic, p.

[36:47] me.

[36:48] Why then do ye not know my word? Because ye cannot hear my word.

[36:49] Ye are from the father, the devil, and the lust of your father do ye desire to do, who from the beginning is a slayer of men, and in the truth standeth not, because the truth is not in him.

[36:50] And when he speaketh untruth, he speaketh from  himself: for he is a liar, and the father of untruth.

[36:51] And I who speak the truth, ye  believe me not.

[36:52] Who of you rebuketh me for a sin? And if I speak the truth, ye  do not believe me.

[36:53] Whosoever is of God heareth the words of God: therefore do  ye not hear, because ye are not of God.

[36:54] The Jews answered and said unto him,  Did we not say well that thou art a Samaritan, and hast demons? Jesus said unto them, As for me, I have not a devil; but my Father do I honour, and ye dishonour  me.

[36:55] I seek not my glory: here is one who seeketh and judgeth.

[37:1] Section XXXVI.

[37:2] Verily, verily, I say unto you, Whosoever keepeth my word shall not see death  for ever.

[37:3] The Jews said unto him, Now we know that thou hast demons.

[37:4] Abraham is dead, and the prophets; and thou sayest, Whosoever keepeth my word shall not  taste death for ever.

[37:5] Art thou haply greater than our father Abraham, who is  dead, and than the prophets, which are dead? whom makest thou thyself? Jesus said unto them, If I glorify myself, my glory is nothing: my Father is he that  glorifieth me; of whom ye say, that he is our God; and yet ye have not known him: but I know him; and if I should say that I know him not, I should become  Arabic, p.

[37:6] a liar like you: but I know him, and keep his word.

[37:7] Abraham your father  longed to see my day; and he saw, and rejoiced.

[37:8] The Jews said unto him,  Thou art now not fifty years old, and hast thou seen Abraham? Jesus said unto  them, Verily, verily, I say unto you, Before Abraham was, I am.

[37:9] And they take stones to stone him: but Jesus concealed himself, and went out of the temple.

[37:10] And he passed through them, and went his way.

[37:11] And as he passed, he saw a man blind from his mother's womb.

[37:12] And his  disciples asked him, and said, Our Master, who sinned, this man, or his parents, so  that he was born blind? Jesus said unto them, Neither did he sin, nor his parents:  but that the works of God may be seen in him.

[37:13] It is incumbent on me to do the deeds of him that sent me, while it is day: a night will come, and no man will be  able to busy himself.

[37:14] As long as I am in the world, I am the light of the world.

[37:15] And when he said that, he spat upon the ground, and made clay of his spittle, and  smeared it on the eyes of the blind man, and said unto him, Go and wash thyself in  the pool of Siloam.

[37:16] And he went and washed, and came seeing.

[37:17] And his neighbours, which saw him of old begging, said, Is not this he that was sitting begging?  And some said, It is he; and others said, Nay, but he resembles him much.

[37:18] He ,  said, I am he.

[37:19] They said unto him, How then were thine eyes opened? He answered and said unto them, A man named Jesus made clay, and smeared it on my eyes, and said unto me, Go and wash in the water of Siloam: and I went and  washed, and received sight.

[37:20] They said unto him, Where is he? He said, I know not.

[37:21] ,  Arabic, p.

[37:22] And they brought him that was previously blind to the Pharisees.

[37:23] And the day in which Jesus made clay and opened with it his eyes was a sabbath  day.

[37:24] And again the Pharisees asked him, How didst thou receive sight? And he said  unto them, He put clay on mine eyes, and I washed, and received sight.

[37:25] The people of the Pharisees said, This man is not from God, for he keepeth not the sabbath.

[37:26] And others said, How can a man that is a sinner do these signs? And there came  to be a division amongst them.

[37:27] And again they said to that blind man, Thou, then, what sayest thou of him that opened for thee thine eyes? He said unto them,  I say that he is a prophet.

[37:28] And the Jews did not believe concerning him, that he was blind, and received sight, until they summoned the parents of him who received  sight, and asked them, Is this your son, of whom ye said that he was born blind?  how then, behold, doth he now see? His parents answered and said, We know  that this is our son, and that he was born blind: but how he has come to see now, or who it is that opened his eyes, we know not: and he also has reached his prime;  ask him, and he will speak for himself.

[37:29] This said his parents, because they were fearing the Jews: and the Jews decided, that if any man should confess of him that  he was the Messiah, they would put him out of the synagogue.

[37:30] For this reason  said his parents, He hath reached his prime; ask him.

[37:31] And they called the man a second time, him that was blind, and said unto him, Praise God: we know that this  man is a sinner.

[37:32] He answered and said unto them, Whether he be a sinner, I know  not: I know one thing, that I was blind, and I now see.

[37:33] They said unto him again,  Arabic, p.

[37:34] What did he unto thee? how opened he for thee thine eyes? He said unto them, I said unto you, and ye did not hear: what wish ye further to hear?  ye also, do ye wish to become disciples to him? And they reviled him, and said unto him, Thou art the disciple of that man; but as for us, we are the disciples of  Moses.

[37:35] And we know that God spake unto Moses: but this man, we know not  whence he is.

[37:36] The man answered and said unto them, From this is the wonder,  because ye know not whence he is, and mine eyes hath he opened.

[37:37] And we know that God heareth not the voice of sinners: but whosoever feareth him, and doeth  his will, him he heareth.

[37:38] From eternity hath it not been heard of, that a man  opened the eyes of a blind man, who had been born in blindness.

[37:39] If then this man  were not from God, he could not do that.

[37:40] They answered and said unto him, Thou wast all of thee born in sins, and dost thou teach us? And they put him forth without.

[37:41] And Jesus heard of his being put forth without, and found him, and said unto  him, Dost thou believe in the Son of God? He that was made whole answered  and said, Who is he, my Lord, that I may believe in him? Jesus said unto him,  Thou hast seen him, and he that speaketh to thee is he.

[37:42] And he said, I believe, my Lord.

[37:43] And he fell down worshipping him.

[38:1] Section XXXVII.

[38:2] And Jesus said, To judge the world am I come, so that they that see not may  see, and they that see may become blind.

[38:3] And some of the Pharisees which were  with him heard that, and they said unto him, Can it be that we are blind? Jesus said unto them, If ye were blind, ye should not have sin: but now ye say, We see: and because of this your sin remaineth.

[38:4] Arabic, p.
